<Text>After getting a crown, I had one of the worst jaw pains. As soon as painkillers would ware off, the pain would come back, and the cycle would start again. At 6pm on a Friday night, Dropbox failed me, or rather my brain, in a fit of obsessive compulsive organizing madness, failed me, and I lost about 7 years of data from my computer. Long story but with no help from Dropbox, I started thinking through all the recent backups I had done - Time Machine, Cloud backups, various hard drives each overwritten and re-used. Desperate, I did a quick Google search and found MacWest which was close to me and open until 8pm on a Friday night. Kaya, in his calm voice, told me to come right over, which I did, dropping off a hard drive to see if any data which had been erased (and overwritten) could be salvaged. Three days later, and equally sleepless nights, Kaya called on Monday to say he had found about 800GB of data. FOUND! I couldn't believe it. I picked up the drive and, yes, despite the lack of file structure, I have been able to slowly piece together what was lost. Some of it I can't find but do I really need auto repair receipts from 2014? So, I am trying to think like Marie Kondo and only care about what's current and meaningful. Kaya made what seemed like the impossible, possible. Thank you, Kaya, and MacWest for outstanding service (and a bit of therapy thrown in)!</review>

< review>
We were really excited to try this place due to the reviews it had. Sadly, customer service isn't their strong point. As soon as I walked in, I was not greeted by staff even though there were 2 at the counter, not even eye contact. Waited a short while after they staff were done talking about their tips (which appeared more important than customer service). After I was helped they had asked if I would like to leave a tip... no offense, but for what?

I am use to higher prices on the coast, but when 2 calzones cost $45 there is a problem. I picked up my order on time but was quite cold when we actually sat down to eat in our room no more than 25 feet away.

<review>(Translated by Google) The fact that the famous tower, completed in 1987, bears some resemblance to the twin towers of the World Trade Center in New York, which were destroyed on September 11, 2001, is because the Fox Plaza was designed by the same architect.
The administration building together with the other towers of Century City can be seen from afar because the surrounding buildings and houses are only a few stories high and are towered over by the high-rise buildings.
This is where the action thriller "Die Hard" (Die Hard) by John McTieman with Alan Rickman as the villain and Bruce Willis as the hero in the main roles was created. In the film, which was released in cinemas in 1988, Fox Plaza was named Nakatomi Plaza.
With this film, Willis made his breakthrough and he played the role of John McCain in four sequels, some of which could not be linked to the success of the first part.
In contrast to Universal Studios, Paramount and Sony, there are unfortunately no public tours.

< Review>
My family and I came here on a Saturday, and it wasn't crowded at all. The staff here are very friendly. They do not speak a lot of English, but just enough to take your orders. We ordered some ramen and sushi, from here, and they were very delicious while not being concentrated. One problem I have is that when I ordered the chicken cutlet ramen bowl, they separated the chicken and the ramen itself. The chicken came after 5 minutes which I didn't like. Despite that, I liked te fact that the cooks did their best to keep their food fresh. Note that when ordering ramen, they give you 4 free California rolls which is awesome. If you're coming here yourself to order ramen and sushi, just order a bowl of ramen. The sushi on the other hand was solid when grabbing it with chopsticks unlike how other restaurants have their sushis. The environment of this place has a good atmosphere, but the place's interior wasn't that good. Overall, I recommend coming to this restaurant. I guarantee that the food will satisfy you.</Review>
